  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c65d11c5-e2f2-48b0-9b68-6b7c614f2f48'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer3465178020054818876">In these eight masterpieces there is no room for the smallest sign of stumbling or youthful undertones: they are perfect. These stories that speak about objects and daily happenings, pass over to another dimension, one of nightmare or revelation. In each text, surprise and uneasiness are ingredients added to the indescribable pleasure of its reading. These stories may upse</span>
  <span id="freeText3465178020054818876" style="display:none">In these eight masterpieces there is no room for the smallest sign of stumbling or youthful undertones: they are perfect. These stories that speak about objects and daily happenings, pass over to another dimension, one of nightmare or revelation. In each text, surprise and uneasiness are ingredients added to the indescribable pleasure of its reading. These stories may upset readers due to a very rare characteristic in literature: They stare at us as if waiting for something in return. After reading these true classics, our opinion of the world cannot remain the same.<br /><br />1. "Casa Tomada" ("House Taken Over")<br />2. " Carta a una señorita en París" (Letter to a Young Lady in Paris")<br />3. "Lejana" ("The Distances")<br />4. "Ómnibus" ("Omnibus")<br />5. "Cefalea" ("Headache")<br />6. "Circe" ("Circe")<br />7. "Las puertas del cielo" ("The Gates of Heaven")<br />8. "Bestiario" ("Bestiary")</span>

Pero el siempre fue mucho mejor en sus cuentos: La Otra Orilla, Los Fuegos el Fuego y Bestiario son los mejores para comenzar. <div id="review_2034636219" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2034636219" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143117-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571421692p2/3143117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2034636219?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/3143117-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9786073147729" href="/book/show/31351038-bestiario">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143117-david?shelf=espa%C3%B1ol">español</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143117-david?shelf=latin-american-lit">latin-american-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143117-david?shelf=argentino">argentino</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2034636219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5034027989390420881"><br/>"We enjoyed the house apart from its spaciousness and it's history ...but it protected the memories of of great grandparents, paternal grandfather, our parents and all of my childhood." Casa tomada (Drunken house)<br/><br/>So the first page starts. A couple cleans the large house everyday trying to make themselves comfortable. Then they start hearing noises. Memories of the past? Monsters? Ghosts? What a great kick off to a collection of haunting tales from Julio Cortázar.<br/><br/>These eight tales range from subt</span>
  <span id="freeText5034027989390420881" style="display:none"><br />"We enjoyed the house apart from its spaciousness and it's history ...but it protected the memories of of great grandparents, paternal grandfather, our parents and all of my childhood." Casa tomada (Drunken house)<br /><br />So the first page starts. A couple cleans the large house everyday trying to make themselves comfortable. Then they start hearing noises. Memories of the past? Monsters? Ghosts? What a great kick off to a collection of haunting tales from Julio Cortázar.<br /><br />These eight tales range from subtle to the plainly twisted. Each story has a unique twist done like only Cortázar can. This is the first collection of short stories published under his real name in 1951.<br /><br />The stories include a bus trip loaded with passengers and their grave site flowers (Ómnibus) to the disturbing Alina Reyes walking the streets of Budapest (Lejana) to the creepy beasts called mancuspias in Cefalea to Delia Mañara, a woman whose two previous boyfriends had died and she in on the third (Circe), the ghostly dancer of Las puertas del cielo, the bizarre vomiting bunnies (Carta a una señorita en París) and finally the curious boy with his intrigue for el mamboretá in Bestiaro.<br /><br />The book can be summed up with Cortázar's own words, "... un balbucear como de gratitud, de innominable aquiescencia."<br /><br />Amen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5034027989390420881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1395853832" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1395853832" />
    <a title="Phyllis Eisenstadt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14351728-phyllis-eisenstadt"><img alt="Phyllis Eisenstadt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535389778p2/14351728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1395853832?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phyllis Eisenstadt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phyllis Eisenstadt" href="/user/show/14351728-phyllis-eisenstadt">Phyllis Eisenstadt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1395853832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1245426690706758594">Julio Cortazar is one of the most famous of the so-called "Boom" authors of Latin America, and with good reason. He is a natural story teller, a natural lover of words, and meticulous in his descriptive details. My favorite story in this collection is "Lejana," which I had read in college for the first time. It is just as interesting and suspenseful the second time around. All of his short stories are excellent and make for enjoyable reading, but some of them are truly outstanding and memorable.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_38812967" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38812967" />
    <a title="Lausº" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1588424-laus"><img alt="Lausº" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518800642p2/1588424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38812967?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lausº" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lausº" href="/user/show/1588424-laus">Lausº</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789681901950" href="/book/show/1374107.Bestiario">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38812967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16879147471270075453">Julio Cortázar escribe ficción, pero con tal elegancia, que te convence que estás leyendo una verdad o por lo menos una "realidad alternativa".<br/><br/>A pesar de que los cuentos fueron escritos con la misma pluma (hablando metafóricamente, porque de lo demás... no me consta) cada uno aborda temas tan distintos sin guardar ninguna familiaridad con el anterior o el siguiente. Además, Cortázar tiene la delicadeza de acomodar las palabras en una forma tan fuera de lo común, que parece que nunca has leído un</span>
  <span id="freeText16879147471270075453" style="display:none">Julio Cortázar escribe ficción, pero con tal elegancia, que te convence que estás leyendo una verdad o por lo menos una "realidad alternativa".<br /><br />A pesar de que los cuentos fueron escritos con la misma pluma (hablando metafóricamente, porque de lo demás... no me consta) cada uno aborda temas tan distintos sin guardar ninguna familiaridad con el anterior o el siguiente. Además, Cortázar tiene la delicadeza de acomodar las palabras en una forma tan fuera de lo común, que parece que nunca has leído un enunciado como ese. Es tan preciso, que cada palabra da en el blanco y permanece una a una hasta que llegas al final de la historia y comienzas la siguiente.<br /><br />De los 8 cuentos, mis favoritos son: La casa tomada, Carta a una señorita en París, Ómnibus y Cirse.<br />&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;&lt;&gt;<br />Cortázar writes fiction, but with such an elegance that convinces you that you're reading the true or at least an "alternate reality".<br /><br />Although all the stories were written with the same pen (metaphorically speaking, because of everything else ... I’m not sure) each one tackles subjects as diverse without saving any familiarity with the previous or next. Also, Cortázar has the delicacy to accommodate the words in a way so unusual, that it seems that you have never read a statement like that. It is so precise that every word is on target and remains one by one until you get to the end of the story and begin the next.<br /><br />Of the 8 stories, my favorites are: La casa tomada, Carta a una señorita en París, Ómnibus and Cirse.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16879147471270075453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_604540908" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/604540908" />
    <a title="Tsuhonets" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10445919-tsuhonets"><img alt="Tsuhonets" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564255234p2/10445919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/604540908?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tsuhonets" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tsuhonets" href="/user/show/10445919-tsuhonets">Tsuhonets</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10445919-tsuhonets?shelf=argentinian">argentinian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10445919-tsuhonets?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10445919-tsuhonets?shelf=short-story">short-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10445919-tsuhonets?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10445919-tsuhonets?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10445919-tsuhonets?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10445919-tsuhonets?shelf=surrealism">surrealism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10445919-tsuhonets?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer604540908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4107600827520183176">This was definitely one interesting work! Weird; but at the same time, extremely, extremely powerful experience. In fact, I feel quite short of words, but I also really want to write about this book.<br/><br/>In these pages there are eight short stories, which Cortázar wrote being inspired by his own nightmares and fears. Sounds cliché. However, it isn't. He truly has captured something here... it's surrealism, horror, fantasy, magical realism, thriller, everything at the same time.<br/><br/>Probably, experience re</span>
  <span id="freeText4107600827520183176" style="display:none">This was definitely one interesting work! Weird; but at the same time, extremely, extremely powerful experience. In fact, I feel quite short of words, but I also really want to write about this book.<br /><br />In these pages there are eight short stories, which Cortázar wrote being inspired by his own nightmares and fears. Sounds cliché. However, it isn't. He truly has captured something here... it's surrealism, horror, fantasy, magical realism, thriller, everything at the same time.<br /><br />Probably, experience really is the best word to describe how the text got to me. There are books, which are thoroughly enjoyable to read, and then there are books which just are experiences. This fits both, but above all, the latter.<br /><br />Trying to disassemble the content, it is probably the very every day nature of these stories, and the delicate way of subtly introducing terror into it, that sucks the reader in. Cortazár's way of writing is very shallow and ambiguous, leading plenty of room foor interpretation and subjective experience.<br /><br />I've always experienced surrealism as something that makes me feel very uneasy, even in some cases slightly fearful. Once it appears that the boundaries of what is <i>supposed</i> to happen are broken, then one becomes to acknowledge that then practically anything could happen. It's not a nice feeling. Yet, even if Kafka has made me feel uncomfortable (that's exactly why I was so into him at one point, the experience was so strong), he has never really intertwined surrealism with horror. These stories are like <i>Metamorphosis</i> taken a bit further.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4107600827520183176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3379264734" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3379264734" />
    <a title="Rhys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1138007-rhys"><img alt="Rhys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442456315p2/1138007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3379264734?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhys" href="/user/show/1138007-rhys">Rhys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781784875855" href="/book/show/48724825-bestiary">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3379264734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer498095990588172096">One of the best collections of short stories I have ever read.<br/><br/>Many of these stories have brilliant intellectual depths but they flow easily and smoothly in a prose that is very different indeed from the glacial prose of Borges, an author that Cortázar is often paired with. Most stories unfold gradually, organically, and they don't allow themselves to be dominated by the core concept that will surely spring a remarkable surprise at the end. Cortázar is extremely good with surprise endings: the tw</span>
  <span id="freeText498095990588172096" style="display:none">One of the best collections of short stories I have ever read.<br /><br />Many of these stories have brilliant intellectual depths but they flow easily and smoothly in a prose that is very different indeed from the glacial prose of Borges, an author that Cortázar is often paired with. Most stories unfold gradually, organically, and they don't allow themselves to be dominated by the core concept that will surely spring a remarkable surprise at the end. Cortázar is extremely good with surprise endings: the twist, wholly unexpected yet absolutely in tune with the inner logic of the story, that suddenly appears in the final few seconds of the reading of the text. <br /><br />So many of the stories in this book are excellent that it is difficult to chose a favourite but I suppose I would have to pick 'The Southern Thruway', which is a remarkable tale about the fragility of civilisation and modern society. It reminded me strongly of the work of J.G. Ballard and J. M. G. Le Clézio but with an extra dimension that I can't quite articulate. Cortázar's prose is never cold or alienating or 'objective'. It is warm and human, even when exploring strange situations that grow more and more bizarre as the action progresses.<br /><br />Other personal highlights, in no especial order, include 'The School at Night'. 'Tara', 'The Gates of Heaven', 'A Yellow Flower'. 'Axolotl' and 'Instructions for John Howell', but there wasn't a bad story in the collection. I am looking forward to reading his novel <i>Hopscotch</i> next.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="498095990588172096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1547180642" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1547180642" />
    <a title="Yvonne (It&#39;s All About Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17970468-yvonne-it-s-all-about-books"><img alt="Yvonne (It&#39;s All About Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491959755p2/17970468.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1547180642?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yvonne (It&#39;s All About Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yvonne (It&#39;s All About Books)" href="/user/show/17970468-yvonne-it-s-all-about-books">Yvonne (It&#39;s All About Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789707311268" href="/book/show/10293567-bestiario">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17970468-yvonne-it-s-all-about-books?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17970468-yvonne-it-s-all-about-books?shelf=read-in-spanish">read-in-spanish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17970468-yvonne-it-s-all-about-books?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17970468-yvonne-it-s-all-about-books?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17970468-yvonne-it-s-all-about-books?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1547180642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1181850131907031150"><a href='https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2016/02/brbestiario.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457377953i/18352802._SX540_.jpg' alt='brbestiario' width='400' height='165' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><strong> Finished reading: February 29th 2016</strong><br/><a href='https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2014/06/35.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433873952i/15152986.jpg' alt='Rating 3,5qqq' width='101' height='26' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><blockquote>
<br/>“Las costumbres, Andrée, son formas concretas del ritmo, son la cuota del ritmo que nos ayuda a vivir. No era tan terrible vomitar conejitos una vez que se había entrado en el ciclo invariable, en el método.”<br/>
</blockquote><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<a href='https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2014/09/myrambles11.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414545099i/11665748.jpg' alt='myrambles1reviewqqq' width='163' height='35' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a><br/><br/>I have been wanting to start reading in Spanish again for ages and it seemed more than fitting to pick an author who comes from the same country I now call my home: Argentina. I have read short stories by <strong>Julio Cortázar</strong> in the pas</span></span>
  <span id="freeText1181850131907031150" style="display:none"><a href="https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2016/02/brbestiario.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457377953i/18352802._SX540_.jpg" alt="brbestiario" width="400" height="165" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><strong> Finished reading: February 29th 2016</strong><br><a href="https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2014/06/35.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433873952i/15152986.jpg" alt="Rating 3,5qqq" width="101" height="26" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><blockquote>
<br>“Las costumbres, Andrée, son formas concretas del ritmo, son la cuota del ritmo que nos ayuda a vivir. No era tan terrible vomitar conejitos una vez que se había entrado en el ciclo invariable, en el método.”<br>
</blockquote><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<a href="https://melovebooks.files.wordpress.com/2014/09/myrambles11.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414545099i/11665748.jpg" alt="myrambles1reviewqqq" width="163" height="35" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>I have been wanting to start reading in Spanish again for ages and it seemed more than fitting to pick an author who comes from the same country I now call my home: Argentina. I have read short stories by <strong>Julio Cortázar</strong> in the past, especially during my years at the University, but I can't remember having read the full<strong> Bestiario</strong> bundle. Like in the other stories I know, <strong>Julio Cortázar</strong> was without doubt an expert in the use of magical realism. The way he was able to combine ordinary things and situations with magical realism elements is what makes his stories so special and I really enjoyed reading them. I do have to say that some stories were better than others; especially <strong>Lejana</strong> didn't really manage to convince me. Still, this is without doubt a very interesting read and it felt good to read in Spanish again.<br><br>I'm doing this review slightly different since there are eight different short stories included in this bundle. Below a short description and my thoughts on each of them.<br><br><strong>Casa Tomada</strong><br><br>In this story a brother and a sister are living in a big and old house in Buenos Aires. It starts as a description of their everyday life; then slowly that same house is being taken over by a 'stranger'. You never get to find out who it was or why they don't try to fight it, and that is part of the charm of this short story.<br><br><strong>Carta A Una Señorita En Paris</strong><br><br>This story is the perfect example of Julio Cortázar's excellent writing skills where he mixed magical realism with interesting descriptions. The main character writes a letter to the owner of the house he has been asked to take care of with a confession: somehow he regularly 'vomits' little rabbits and then has to hide them... It sounds absurd but it is actually a quite funny story.<br><br><strong>Lejana</strong><br><br>This one is without doubt my least favorite story. I normally like magical realism, but this story was too confusing to be enjoyable. It seems to be a story of a woman who writes about some kind of visions, but to be honest I'm still not completely sure what was really going on.<br><br><strong>Ómnibus</strong><br><br>One of my favorites of this bundle. What I love is that Julio Cortázar used ordinary things like a bus ride and changes it into a surreal story. Having lived in BA and taken the same 168 bus many times only improves the reading experience...<br><br><strong>Cefalea</strong><br><br>This story is a bit more fantastical than others and is actually quite interesting. The characters have to take care of fictional animals (mancuspias) but are struggling because they are suffering from really bad headaches. Slowly things are starting to go wrong and they don't know how to fix it..<br><br><strong>Cirse</strong><br><br>This story made me crave chocolate! Delia makes chocolates and saw her two previous boyfriends die under suspicious circumstances. Mario prefers to ignore the odds and is determined to be her third and only living boyfriend... An interesting enough story for sure.<br><br><strong>Las Puertas Del Cielo</strong><br><br>This story hasn't as many magical realism elements but is without doubt very interesting as well. One of the main characters is a husband who is struggling to coope with the death of his wife, and his friend is trying to help him. One night when they go to a milonga he thinks he sees his dead wife again... Las Puertas Del Cielo turned out to be intriguing and also has a nice reference to the whole milonga culture.<br><br><strong>Bestiario</strong><br><br>The last story is probably the most famous one and is also the story the bundle has been named after. I remember having to read this particular short story back in Uni and I really enjoyed reading it second time around. Magical realism at its best! The characters live in a big house and there also happens to be a tiger walking around. The movements of the characters are limited by the tiger, but they seem to be used to it... Until someone makes a mistake. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>P.S. Find more of my reviews <a href="http://melovebooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1181850131907031150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1998900139" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1998900139" />
    <a title="Quiver" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9310150-quiver"><img alt="Quiver" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489326638p2/9310150.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1998900139?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Quiver" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Quiver" href="/user/show/9310150-quiver">Quiver</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781860464270" href="/book/show/2266703.Bestiary">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9310150-quiver?shelf=a-english">a-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9310150-quiver?shelf=f-in-translation">f-in-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9310150-quiver?shelf=s-short-stories">s-short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1998900139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13037981609636712165">I wouldn't confess my secret either.<br/><blockquote>I have never described this to you before, not so much, I don’t think, from the lack of truthfulness as that, just naturally, one is not going to explain to people at large that from time to time one vomits up a small rabbit.<br/><br/>—<i>Letter of a Young Lady in Paris</i></blockquote><br/>If Jorge Luis Borges is the literary scientist who excels at exhibiting impossible geometries in miniature, Julio Cortázar is the long-winded, mussy-haired standup act with something direly unsettling about </span>
  <span id="freeText13037981609636712165" style="display:none">I wouldn't confess my secret either.<br /><blockquote>I have never described this to you before, not so much, I don’t think, from the lack of truthfulness as that, just naturally, one is not going to explain to people at large that from time to time one vomits up a small rabbit.<br /><br />—<i>Letter of a Young Lady in Paris</i></blockquote><br />If Jorge Luis Borges is the literary scientist who excels at exhibiting impossible geometries in miniature, Julio Cortázar is the long-winded, mussy-haired standup act with something direly unsettling about each of his stories, something you really want to pin down, but—no matter how closely you listen—you never will.<br /><blockquote>When I feel that I’m going to bring up a rabbit, I put two fingers in my mouth like an open pincer, and I wait to feel the lukewarm fluff rise in my throat …</blockquote><br />For those unfamiliar with Borges, perhaps I should be playing on a comparison with another short-piece writer closer to the Western ear who was also Cortázar's contemporary: E. B. White.<br /><br />Surprised?<br /><br />Julio Cortázar (1914–1984) was an Argentine writer, and part of the flourishing Latin American literary scene of the 50s and 60s.<br /><br />E. B. White (1899–1985) was na American writer, known for his contributions to the <i>The New Yorker </i>all of which are firmly grounded in reality. (Although, of course, there's his fiction for children, such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24178.Charlotte_s_Web" title="Charlotte's Web by E.B. White" rel="nofollow noopener"> Charlotte's Web</a>.) My literary-minded readers will know him for the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33514.The_Elements_of_Style" title="The Elements of Style by William Strunk Jr." rel="nofollow noopener"> The Elements of Style</a> writing manual that contains such classical advice as <i>Omit needless words</i>,<i> Be clear</i>, and<i> Place yourself in the background.</i><br /><br />Now for the comparison.<br /><br />Within the bastion of brilliant writing, Cortázar is the polar opposite of White.<br /><br />Let me spell that out:<br /> <br />	 1. Cortázar does <i>not </i>omit needless words, <br />	 2. Cortázar is <i>not </i>clear, <br />	 3. Cortázar does <i>not</i> place himself (or, rather, the narrator) in the background. <br /> <br />The first point speaks of Cortázar’s style: easygoing, seemingly unedited, discursive, transferring meaning through hints and through osmosis rather than at the edge of a blade. However, he doesn’t resort to a wordiness common to the preceding ages, such as the fin de siècle cloying headiness brought upon by (the just demonstrated type of) adjectival pile-up. Also, the French <i>conte cruel, </i>which explores similar phenomena, namely the “cruel” twists of fate (albeit usually socially distasteful, grotesque, appalling, bizarre), does so either explicitly or opaquely, but it doesn’t leave you wondering what just happened. Your curiosity is extinguished because you are satisfied, or because you don't care. Not with Cortázar.<br /><br />The second point speaks of Cortázar’s subject matter: he treats the impossibly, subtly nightmarish that gets under your skin without you knowing why. It is ill-defined, indefinite, indescribably balanced on the boundaries of perception. Some of his stories could be called Dahlesque (or indeed some of Roald Dahl’s stories, like <i>
  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Jelly_(short_story)" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Royal Jelly</a>
</i>, come close to what is found in Cortázar’s <em>Bestiary</em>), but where Dahl gives you the satisfaction of a clear, if distinctly disturbing ending, Cortázar usually does not. Like in Borges’s <i>There Are More Things, </i><a href="https://quiverquotes.com/2017/09/29/describing-the-ineffable/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">you are left wondering what you would have seen</a> had the camera panned the other way.<br /><br />The third point is arguably the hardest to transfer from non-fiction to fiction. I’ll make the transference anyway: in fiction, <i>place yourself in the background </i>means <i>leave the narrative surface unbroken</i>. In other words, let the reader skate over all the mechanisms, issues, trickery that underly successful fiction; let them enjoy the scenery. Cracks in the narrative surface, hills and ravines, narrative surfaces within narrative surfaces, warped reflections and startling linguistic legerdemain are the domain of magical realism and metafiction. Cortázar offers one or both admirably.<br /><blockquote>(it’s almost lovely to see how they like to stand on their hind legs, nostalgia for that so-distant humanity, perhaps an imitation of their god walking about and looking at them darkly; besides which, you will have observed — when you were a baby, perhaps — that you can put a bunny in the corner against the wall like a punishment, and he’ll stand there, paws against the wall and very quiet, for hours and hours)</blockquote><br />Aren't you yearning to find out how the rabbit conclave ends?</span>
  <a data-text-id="13037981609636712165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_197477953" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197477953" />
    <a title="Néstor Silverio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6016567-n-stor-silverio"><img alt="Néstor Silverio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500327809p2/6016567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_3095888660" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3095888660" />

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3095888660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer110273571036126288">There’s nothing like Argentinian short stories. From Borges to Mariana Enriquez, there’s always something way too real to the fantastic world created by these authors. Cortazar presents us a universe of wonder with humane emotions in bestial situations or the opposite. The use of the fantastic is either a metaphor or a reality to portray the absurdity of existence itself.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_561832967" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/561832967" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4437626-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597081378p2/4437626.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/561832967?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/4437626-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/16082578-besti-rio">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer561832967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10324942043668030231">3/5<br/><br/>High expectations lead to higher disappointments; however, as much as I admire Cortázar, this book in particular did not have that much of an interesting premise for me to begin with. Why did I read it? Ruling out my ownership of both this book and a vast amount of free time, I was intrigued with the way Cortázar would perform in his genre of preference, short quotidian stories laced together with supernatural elements. Despite my devotion to the author, I do not share his liking for these wo</span>
  <span id="freeText10324942043668030231" style="display:none">3/5<br /><br />High expectations lead to higher disappointments; however, as much as I admire Cortázar, this book in particular did not have that much of an interesting premise for me to begin with. Why did I read it? Ruling out my ownership of both this book and a vast amount of free time, I was intrigued with the way Cortázar would perform in his genre of preference, short quotidian stories laced together with supernatural elements. Despite my devotion to the author, I do not share his liking for these works, much too brief, in my opinion, to give a well-rounded view or a consistent character definition, unless, of course, the character, opinion or trait in the works is the sole axis for each construction as a whole. In his Bestiario, Julio Cortázar offers an eclectic collection of stories with little in common except for the aforementioned supernatural essence and - luckily - his astounding way with words. However, I was lacking in a connection between all of them (they ranged from plain to scary to absolutely obscure) and the disparity in the quality between the worst and best was dismal, in my opinion. I see myself recommending the individual stories "Ómnibus" and "Bestiario" in the future, but I would leave the entire thing for Cortázar devotees only. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10324942043668030231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Benoît" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8593248-beno-t"><img alt="Benoît" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538568913p2/8593248.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3072689887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5274696933622764346">This is his first collection of shorts and it is a funny beast. Innocent, delicate and gracious by themselves, the stories share a similar pattern by featuring an irrational element casting an air of mystery and unsettlement over them. It creates a deliciously unique tone that I have not encountered before. It plays with your mind, it is not scary but rather surrealistic, imaginative, enigmatic. The "element" is always different, open to many interpretations, and I'd lie if I said the stories we</span>
  <span id="freeText5274696933622764346" style="display:none">This is his first collection of shorts and it is a funny beast. Innocent, delicate and gracious by themselves, the stories share a similar pattern by featuring an irrational element casting an air of mystery and unsettlement over them. It creates a deliciously unique tone that I have not encountered before. It plays with your mind, it is not scary but rather surrealistic, imaginative, enigmatic. The "element" is always different, open to many interpretations, and I'd lie if I said the stories were homogeneous (Lejana, Circe, Las Puertas del Cielo interested me distinctly less). </span>
  <a data-text-id="5274696933622764346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2404764743" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2404764743" />
    <a title="Ricardo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12748651-ricardo"><img alt="Ricardo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347402554p2/12748651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2404764743?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ricardo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ricardo" href="/user/show/12748651-ricardo">Ricardo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789896232054" href="/book/show/25406428-besti-rio">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12748651-ricardo?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2404764743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14161675623603403813">This is a compilation of tales by Cortazar. Each tale portrays the mind tribulations and relationship tensions of the human existence in very distinct ways.<br/>In, most of, the tales animals are used as allegories/metaphors of a person's feelings (guilt, sense of loss) but detailed in a very intense form.<br/>Cortazar writes in some cases in a way similar to the fantastic scenarios of his fellowman Borges.<br/>An interesting entry point to the work of Cortazar.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2328658647" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2328658647" />
    <a title="Robert Frecer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69489105-robert-frecer"><img alt="Robert Frecer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570834033p2/69489105.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2328658647?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert Frecer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert Frecer" href="/user/show/69489105-robert-frecer">Robert Frecer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781784875855" href="/book/show/48724825-bestiary">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2328658647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14630963694084129227">A weird mix of Dušan Mitana and Stephen King written with flourish and creativity. Even though they were published 80-50 years ago, the stories feel absolutely contemporary. Cortazar is a master of foreshadowing and subtle humor; reading this was a delight.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZMWzRNxBZo+HYQkF8i/oEQpekipocy/4xaMpHt/vw+LauuWmNpNB3FL2qnmwEW5fiTUvrcXsPfgDg29MNBz/3Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('d6UdUpnvj4/6rpw3eZ2z1LofOalRrho/KoJuKmYjHYHJ2kuwcz2o3C85P0s7ozWaOXSELvwxCD/soih4jdAhvg==')})
  }

Hubo muchos muertos, de los cuales sólo siete cayeron<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText12628778663036249745\" style=\"display:none\">El 9 de junio de 1956 los generales Tanco y Valle se sublevaron contra el gobierno de facto que había destituido a Perón en septiembre de 1955. El levantamiento fue reprimido brutal e ilegalmente. Hubo muchos muertos, de los cuales sólo siete cayeron en acción. En los basurales de José León Suárez, un grupo de civiles -algunos de ellos relacionados vagamente con la conspiración; el resto, ajeno por completo a ella- fueron masacrados antes incluso de que fuera dictada la ley marcial. Unos pocos lograron escapar de la muerte, a duras penas. En 1957, Rodolfo Walsh emprendió la investigación de estos hechos, cuyos resultados publicó en forma de notas en el diario &quot;Mayoría&quot; y, poco después, como libro.\n\n&quot;Operación Masacre&quot;, una de las primeras novelas de &quot;no ficción&quot; escritas en castellano, se anticipó en nueve años al New Journalism, es decir, la aplicación de procedimientos propios del género Edición especial: literatura complementaria.\nNi de paz ni de amor. La noche que abre El Eternauta es de angustia y desolación. La nevada que cae sobre Buenos Aires es sólo el primer tramo de una invasión alieníge<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText14953426707800433270\" style=\"display:none\">El Eternauta: La historieta original. Edición especial: literatura complementaria.\nNi de paz ni de amor. La noche que abre El Eternauta es de angustia y desolación. La nevada que cae sobre Buenos Aires es sólo el primer tramo de una invasión alienígena que desgranará sobre reconocibles escenarios urbanos su violenta espiral de poesía y aniquilamiento. ¿Cómo se combate esta estratégica avanzada militar que ahoga las esperanzas de supervivencia humana? ¿Dónde se esconde el verdadero enemigo? ¿Quién será capaz de enfrentar un destino peor que la muerte? ¿Qué hacer cuando es imposible avanzar e inviable retroceder? Resistir. Contra el invasor. O contra el ejercicio abusivo del poder, que viene a ser lo mismo.\n\nLa mayor aventura de ciencia-ficción escrita en el sur del mundo apareció serializada como un largo folletín en la revista Hora Cero Semanal entre 1957 y 1959. Obra de Héctor Germán Oesterheld y Francisco Solano López, la epopeya de El Eternauta es una minuciosa radiografía de la historia argentina de los últimos cincuenta años. Metáfora alucinante del país arrasado, entregado a los intereses externos y dominado por el invasor. Una historia actual que continúa gritando su mensaje a los cuatro vientos: Cuando ya no importa si se gana o se pierde, lo único que prevalece es la dignidad con la cual se presente batalla.<\/span>\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25824.Julio_Cort_zar">About Julio Cortázar</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/25824.Julio_Cort_zar"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1496948373p3/25824.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/25824.Julio_Cort_zar">Julio Cortázar
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,618
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5871189439419789465">Julio Cortázar, born Julio Florencio Cortázar Descotte, was an Argentine author of novels and short stories. He influenced an entire generation of Latin American writers from Mexico to Argentina, and most of his best-known work was written in France, where he established himself in 1951.</span>

</div>
</div>
